    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText15254794328246234028" style="display:none"><p>It’s been a year since Eden last spoke to Tyler. She remains furious at him for leaving her and has moved on with life in Chicago, where she is at University studying psychology. As school breaks up for the summer, she heads back to Santa Monica, but she’s not the only one with that idea…<br /></p><p>Despite their break-up and Tyler’s abrupt departure last summer, is there something Tyler is keeping from Eden? Are they both as over each other as they thought, and could Eden even begin to forgive Tyler?<br /></p><p>In <em>Did I Mention I Miss You?</em>, the explosive finale to Estelle Maskame’s phenomenal DIMILY trilogy, can Tyler and Eden finally work things out, against all the odds?<br /></p></span>

  <i>***4 "Finally, finally, finally!!!" stars***</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481043229i/21378706.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Finally, we took the ending of this wonderful series and i can say that this book repaid me for all the pain that i had to get through the previous two books and at the beginning of this one!!!!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449683732ra/17324120.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>The DIMILY trilogy was a rough ride full of heartbreaking, desperation and sadness, but it gave us a great insight in family matters, addiction and abuse problems, teenager behaviour.... and through all of these ugly things a great, forbidden and complicated</span>
  <span id="freeText14516493729844538681" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>***4 "Finally, finally, finally!!!" stars***</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481043229i/21378706.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, we took the ending of this wonderful series and i can say that this book repaid me for all the pain that i had to get through the previous two books and at the beginning of this one!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449683732ra/17324120.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The DIMILY trilogy was a rough ride full of heartbreaking, desperation and sadness, but it gave us a great insight in family matters, addiction and abuse problems, teenager behaviour.... and through all of these ugly things a great, forbidden and complicated love has bloom...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378707.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"People deserve second chances!!!"</i>
</b><br><br>At the end of the previous book, Tyler got overwhelmed by everything that took place when he and Eden revealed their relationship to their family and friends and he just snapped and run away... but not before, he promised to Eden that he will return back for her!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378708.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>But Eden's heart broke and her happiness shattered by his disappearance but also by all those things that she had to deal with, alone, without Tyler by her side.... <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378709.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"But I don’t want to wait. I spent months waiting, wondering and guessing and driving myself insane as the days rolled into months and the months rolled into a year. I gave up on waiting a long time ago. I gave up on him a long time ago."</i>
</b><br><br>Now, after a whole year, Eden is back in L.A. and she is dealing with the complications from their love.... Her family is falling apart and both her father and Jamie have an awful attitude toward her and everywhere she goes everybody is whispering behind her back about her relationship with her stepbrother!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378710.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Eden is feeling ashamed and betrayed by Tyler... He just left her to deal with everything all alone and he is living his life somewhere else!!!<br>She was waiting for him, but he never came back and then she just gave up on him and their love!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378711.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Now, she is feeling only anger for him and nothing more....<br><br><b>
  <i>"I don’t hate Tyler. I might have told Rachael that over the past year, but it’s a lie. I might have told Ella that I never wanted to see him again, but I’ve realized that’s a lie too. I could never hate him. I’m just . . . mad. I am mad at the fact that I no longer feel the way I used to and I am mad at him for making me feel this way."</i>
</b><br><br>But now, Tyler is deciding to come back and to claim Eden for once again...<br>For him, nothing is over and even though that he is hurting inside by Eden's rejection, he won't give up on her....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378712.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>So, he is insisting for her to follow him back home because he wants to show her how he spent the time that they were apart....<br><br><b>
  <i>“There’s nothing to talk about,” I say.<br>“There’s everything to talk about.”<br>He’s right: There is everything to talk about. I just don’t want to."</i>
</b><br><br><i>Will Eden shut him out for good or will she give him a chance to prove himself???<br>Will she understand his reasons why he had to leave and start a new life away from her???<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378713.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Will their love are irreparable broken or they can find their way back to each other???<br>And how will they deal with their family and the rejections that they are having for them???<br>Will they fight to be together or will they give up???</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378714.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Maybe Tyler and I are done, not because we’re not in love with one another, but because we are an impossible pair."</i>
</b> <i>{Eden}</i><br><br><b>
  <i>“I’m sorry... I shouldn’t have ruined all of this, and do you know what the worst part is? I don’t know if I can fix it, and I don’t think you want me to.”</i>
</b> <i>{Tyler}</i><br><br>For once again, i liked Eden but damn, in the half book i was so mad with her....<br>First of all, because she was acting like she did something very wrong and terrible...<br>When you have made your choice, you have to defend her!!! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Also, she gave up on Tyler so easily and i didn't like that because he had much more problems to deal with than her....<br>Yep, it was shitty that she had to deal with all this negative behaviour all alone, but give to that man some credits!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447856797ra/17058651.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"I don’t know what to say or how to feel. But my heart is beating painfully with a sense of longing. For all that I have convinced myself that I hate Tyler, the truth is that I have just missed him. I’ve missed hearing his voice and seeing him smirk and feeling his touch. I’ve missed Tyler and there’s no denying it now, but things are complicated."</i>
</b><br><br>God, i loveeeee Tyler!!! I loved him from the first time when he was the biggest asshole on earth, but in every book, I loved him even more...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>He had many issues to solve and he did such a great job!!!<br>This man in this book wasn't anything like the boy we met in the first book!!!<br>He had matured so much and he became such a wonderful man.... and God, his love for Eden was so big and he never gave up on her and that was admirable!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478393270ra/21068174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“I know I’ve messed up before and I’ve made some fucked-up decisions... but the truth is, I’ve always had a choice. I chose to throw my life away when I could have chosen to do something positive about it instead. New York and the tour were a start... but that wasn’t enough, which is why I had to leave, Eden. I didn’t want to keep making mistakes. I wanted to be a better person, not because I owed it to you, but because I owed it to myself.”</i>
</b><br><br>Eden and Tyler was made for each other and when they were together everything was absolutely awesome!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378717.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I liked how the things turned out in here.... They deserved the happiness after all the shits that they went through all those years!!!!<br>I liked very much what they built together in every aspect....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378718.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>"It’s over, Tyler’s telling Dad.<br>We’re done, I’ve told Tyler.<br>But maybe it’s not.<br>Maybe we’re not."</i>
</b><br><br>For once again, i will speak about their family....<br>Both the mothers were such amazing and full of understanding creatures and i love them both very much!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464192658ra/19210913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Chase was just an innocent child with pure heart!!!<br>But Jamie was such a difficult child... He was no better than Tyler in the first book and his attitude toward Eden and Tyler was pissing me off very badly....<br>And for once again, i will speak for Eden's asshole of father... God, in every book was worst than the previous one.... I wanted to put some sense inside his full of shit head!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474533352ra/20611067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"Real families don’t hate one another like we do. Real families aren’t as strained as we are. Real families don’t have to deal with the stepkids falling in love like Tyler and I did...<br>I guess in a way we’re all just broken pieces, hoping somehow to fit together to become a perfect picture, a real family. But that will never happen. We will never, ever fit."</i>
</b><br><br>And that was the end of a bittersweet, heartbroken at times but also a very wonderful journey!!!<br>I will miss these guys very much!!!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481043229ra/21378719.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>"It’s not wrong for us to feel the way we do. It’s not wrong for us to be together. From day one, we have never, ever been wrong.<br>Maybe these past three years we’ve been fighting so hard to get everyone else to accept our relationship when the only two people who needed to accept it us was ourselves.<br>And after all this time, I think we finally have."</i>
</b></span>

<div id="review_1694609119" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1694609119" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16000959-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577987193p2/16000959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1694609119?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/16000959-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26251365-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1694609119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6093851782672178217">It's the final part of the <i>Did I Mention I Love You?</i> trilogy. We made it. Eden's going home for the summer. Home isn't what it used to be. It's where she's now the talk of the town for all the wrong reasons, she alone dealing with the fallout of her and Tyler's relationship, the gossip on people's lips. He always said he'd come back - but what happens when he does and she's moved on? The pain has been replaced by anger.<br/><br/><i>Did I Mention I Miss You?</i> is just as readable as all the other books. Had I n</span>
  <span id="freeText6093851782672178217" style="display:none">It's the final part of the <i>Did I Mention I Love You?</i> trilogy. We made it. Eden's going home for the summer. Home isn't what it used to be. It's where she's now the talk of the town for all the wrong reasons, she alone dealing with the fallout of her and Tyler's relationship, the gossip on people's lips. He always said he'd come back - but what happens when he does and she's moved on? The pain has been replaced by anger.<br /><br /><i>Did I Mention I Miss You?</i> is just as readable as all the other books. Had I not had actual plans over the weekend, this would have been finished days ago, because apparently reading when people want to talk to you is a rude thing. So, here we are.<br /><br /><a href="https://heatherwrites.co.uk/2016/02/14/review-did-i-mention-i-love-you-estelle-maskame/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>DIMILY</i>
</a> was good and addictive, yet had its issues in the genre in the sense that it bowed to the bad-boy-good-girl tropes (I have long waited for books to dodge these tropes, but have rarely enjoyed a book so much alongside them as I did here); <a href="https://heatherwrites.co.uk/2016/02/27/review-did-i-mention-i-need-you-estelle-maskame/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>DIMINY</i>
</a> wrapped it all up in a neat little package where it maturely picked apart the co-dependency and took the series in a direction I didn't imagine, but inside hoped (hurrah, someone did it!). So rather than fall immediately into the series wholeheartedly, I fell in with a few final cards kept to my chest, a few points that I held out on - bit by bit, the series took them all and handled them. I raved about the ending of the second book far and wide. Seriously, ask anyone who's been around me these last few months.<br /><br />So the third had me intrigued. <i>DIMIMY</i> almost removed the couple. It's not just about them - it's never just about them. Their families are falling apart, relationships strained, people striking out. Marriages are on the brink of collapse, parents coming into fire whether rightly or wrongly. Even friendships start to wobble: <i>I thought you meant what you said?</i><br /><br />The DIMILY trilogy is, basically, really good. It's readable, it fits in the genre, but it also takes it all on in a way you hope others do. It gets ugly. People need to find and be themselves, not be part of a pair. They stand their ground. Most impressively, they grow. Three years in three books, and they all grow. <br /><br />So yes, they were head over heels mindlessly as teenagers, but move it forward a few years and it's all different.<br /><br />It's been a while since I finished a book series. It's been a while since I did so and felt sad. It's definitely the first time I've followed a couple through a series with such speed, and y'know, I think I might miss having these books to look forward to. <i>DIMIMY</i> is definitely worth the wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6093851782672178217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1799208839" />
    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1799208839?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31826238-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7591340-sarah-elizabeth?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1799208839" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2675419083279006980">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to SOURCEBOOKS Fire and NetGalley.)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The biggest difference between your dad and Tyler?” Mom says quietly. She hesitates for only a moment. “Your dad never came back.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This was a YA contemporary romance which picked up a year after the previous book.<br/><br/>I felt quite sorry for Eden in this book as it seemed like she’d had to put up with a lot during the course of a year, whilst Tyler had just left and put everything but Eden behind h</span>
  <span id="freeText2675419083279006980" style="display:none">(I received an advance copy of this book for free. Thanks to SOURCEBOOKS Fire and NetGalley.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The biggest difference between your dad and Tyler?” Mom says quietly. She hesitates for only a moment. “Your dad never came back.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>This was a YA contemporary romance which picked up a year after the previous book.<br><br>I felt quite sorry for Eden in this book as it seemed like she’d had to put up with a lot during the course of a year, whilst Tyler had just left and put everything but Eden behind him.<br><br>The storyline in this was about Eden and Tyler meeting up again after a year apart, and having to decide where their relationship would go, especially given how against the relationship it seemed Eden’s father was. I did feel like it took a while for the book to really get going though, and there wasn’t enough romance for me, as the story was more about the arguments and conflict than the romance. <br><br>The ending to this was happy though, and I was pleased for Eden and Tyler.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433081147i/15047180.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6.5 out of 10</span>
  <a data-text-id="2675419083279006980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1580646426" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1580646426" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27878270-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598292911p2/27878270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1580646426?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/27878270-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26251365-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27878270-wendy?shelf=my-bookshelf">my-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1580646426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3428580027523439890">Did I Mention I Miss You was one of my most anticipated reads of 2016 and when it released I instantly bought the ebook (and the physical copy of course) and started reading it. Unfortunately, I got into a reading slump the next day and that one lasted for one month. It was upsetting, but I’m glad I finally got to read it.<br/><br/>When I started reading Did I Mention I Miss You, I didn’t have any problems getting used to Eden again; it was pretty easy actually. In DIMILY and DIMINY it was easy for me to </span>
  <span id="freeText3428580027523439890" style="display:none">Did I Mention I Miss You was one of my most anticipated reads of 2016 and when it released I instantly bought the ebook (and the physical copy of course) and started reading it. Unfortunately, I got into a reading slump the next day and that one lasted for one month. It was upsetting, but I’m glad I finally got to read it.<br /><br />When I started reading Did I Mention I Miss You, I didn’t have any problems getting used to Eden again; it was pretty easy actually. In DIMILY and DIMINY it was easy for me to read from Eden’s perspective and while I couldn’t particularly relate to her, I felt a deep connection. And I could feel that connection when I was reading DIMIMY too. It’s unique to have such a special bonding with a character.<br /><br />And when we’re talking about characters, let’s talk about Tyler. Because he totally amazed me – throughout the whole book. Comparing him with his nineteen year old self (DIMIMY) or even his seventeen year old self (DIMILY) he has grown so much. His character development and personality change totally did it for me. I actually really hated Tyler in DIMILY, but I must say.. he really is a grown man in DIMIMY. I’ve never seen such a development and I loved how he turned out to be.<br /><br />I was really skeptical about the whole Tyden drama when I started reading DIMIMY because I was so shocked about the ending of DIMINY. I totally gave up on them since then, so I didn’t really know what to expect from DIMIMY. I was also very skeptical about Eden’s feelings; being so freaking mad to Tyler but still having feelings for him. In some kind of way it wasn’t realistic in my point of view.<br /><br />I loved that they went to Portland this time. It’s a new city to discover (at least for me, it wasn’t for Eden and Tyler) and I liked to read about something different than the good old Santa Monica. I liked the way Estelle described all the surroundings; it was detailed, but not that detailed and that balanced it out perfectly.<br /><br />One thing I miss in Did I Mention I Miss You is the original casting. Sure, it’s most likely groups fall apart (I also saw it happen in real life) but I just missed the whole group. Their adventures, their parties.. it felt like I missed a small part of the story because of that. Overall, I do like the new group. They’re all on the same page and just nice to each other - I don’t know how to describe it another way.<br /><br />The thing that disappointed me the most in Did I Mention I Miss You was the drama. Let’s be honest, DIMILY and DIMINY are full of drama (you guys all know how much I love drama) and I missed that in DIMIMY. It kind of had an anti climax feel to it and I pity that. I don’t want to spoil, so I’ll keep it vague, but one thing happened and I expected something big and dramatic to happen, but it didn’t. It just didn’t. Even the ending wasn’t full of climax or that dramatic and it didn’t make it memorable at all. And I just feel sorry for it.<br /><br />So overall, I really liked this book. It was easy to read and I loved the character development and the writing. The only thing I didn’t like was the ending and the anti climax feel. So that’s why I give it four stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3428580027523439890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

<span id="freeTextContainer5562177925134751275">I CAN'T BELIEVE IT'S OVER!<br/><br/>Wow. These books were a complete thrill from start to finish. Tyler's character development is like no other and I was so overwhelmed with happiness when we found out about the youth centre. I'm so happy Estelle made the decision to bring Tyler "back to health" and let him get help as it's something that could inspire anyone reading that it is possible to start <br/><br/>But I'm so happy we went from "Silence ensues. And it's so unbelievably awkward and uncomfortable that I think</span>
  <span id="freeText5562177925134751275" style="display:none">I CAN'T BELIEVE IT'S OVER!<br /><br />Wow. These books were a complete thrill from start to finish. Tyler's character development is like no other and I was so overwhelmed with happiness when we found out about the youth centre. I'm so happy Estelle made the decision to bring Tyler "back to health" and let him get help as it's something that could inspire anyone reading that it is possible to start <br /><br />But I'm so happy we went from "Silence ensues. And it's so unbelievably awkward and uncomfortable that I think I could cry. How did it end up like this? How did we get here?" from the start of the book to "I'm smiling against his lips because my happiness in that moment is so overwhelming that I just can't control it anymore." at the end. IT MAKES ME SO HAPPY BECAUSE TYLER AND EDEN DESERVE SO MUCH HAPPINESS. They've finally accepted their situation, as has everyone around them, and it makes me so happy because I didn't think there was anything wrong with their situation in the first place; they're not related. <br /><br />Though I did feel as if everything happened too fast after Tyler came back into the picture. Eden went from hating him to loving him and put her trust in him SO fast and I get it because love but it felt rushed when you put it into perspective. And the shooeessssss! Eden brought the converse out again and aghhh I loved that symbol for them so much. <br /><br />I don't really have much to say because all I have is happiness bubbling inside of me from how Eden sorted things out with her dad and how she and Tyler are together and how cute Chase is and from Tyler being honest with Ella about his dad and just everything. I'm so happy. But I could edit this later when the happiness has dissipated and make it into a real review but we'll just see. <br /><br />I'm also so sad I've finished with this trilogy, I was SO invested in it and it's rare for me to find a book I want to be attached to every second of the day. I hope Estelle writes an epilogue in the form of a novella in the future because I think that would be nice. But aside from that, a definite 5/5 for this book and the series. I loved every single aspect of it and I would definitely recommend to anyone. </span>

<div id="review_2398073134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2398073134" />
    <a title="Natalia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52662522-natalia"><img alt="Natalia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485879776p2/52662522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2398073134?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalia" href="/user/show/52662522-natalia">Natalia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492632214" href="/book/show/28321049-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52662522-natalia?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2398073134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14809355073332045690">It’s quite ridiculous how fast I read this book. Right after I finished the second one I started this one and I read it in one night. The book was really addicting and entertaining.<br/>The book takes place one year after Tyler leaves. During this time Eden hasn’t had any contact with him what so ever and is left alone to deal with the mess they made last summer. She has convinced herself that she’s not in love with Tyler anymore and she’s really mad at him. Everything changes when he suddenly shows </span>
  <span id="freeText14809355073332045690" style="display:none">It’s quite ridiculous how fast I read this book. Right after I finished the second one I started this one and I read it in one night. The book was really addicting and entertaining.<br />The book takes place one year after Tyler leaves. During this time Eden hasn’t had any contact with him what so ever and is left alone to deal with the mess they made last summer. She has convinced herself that she’s not in love with Tyler anymore and she’s really mad at him. Everything changes when he suddenly shows up.<br />Tyler in this book was a lot more mature and calm, it was great to see that he has finally put the past behind him and he’s trying to be better. I was really proud of him for going to therapy.<br />I totally understand why he had to leave, but he couldn’t have seriously expected that everything would be all right. Eden had every right to be mad.<br />Tyler and Eden were really cute in this book. Especially Tyler has grown up a lot during the 3 years and it’s really nice to see, how in the end he turned out to be really great.<br />I have mixed opinions about the end. I get that the author tried to make the end as happy as possible, but I don’t think all that was necessary. I mean Tyler being in contact with the father that abused him?!? I know that it’s explained and all, but just don’t think that it was necessary. Same thing with Eden’s father. In the end they don’t exactly get on, but their relationship is a bit better. I just find it unnecessary, it’s okay not to have a perfect relationship with your father. Family is important, but when someone is acting as a jerk the whole time, you’re not obligated to get on with them.<br />Overall this was a fun series and I’m glad I read it. I would recommended if you are looking for a light contemporary, but be aware that sometimes the main character can be annoying and make really irrational decisions so if you get easily annoyed it’s definitely not the book for you. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14809355073332045690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79111408-brinley?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79111408-brinley?shelf=september-2020-challenge">september-2020-challenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer12681244421642865316">I need to stop saying I'm going to stop reading this series, because at this point, I'm just lying to myself. Every time I'm looking for a quick read late at night, this series shows up conveniently, and its available from the library every time. <br/><br/>The stepsibling romance might throw some people off, and I do have to admit that I do find it weird, even though they're not related at all. I mainly just find myself ignoring that they're stepsiblings, which is fairly easy. Eden and Tyler's romance has</span>
  <span id="freeText12681244421642865316" style="display:none">I need to stop saying I'm going to stop reading this series, because at this point, I'm just lying to myself. Every time I'm looking for a quick read late at night, this series shows up conveniently, and its available from the library every time. <br /><br />The stepsibling romance might throw some people off, and I do have to admit that I do find it weird, even though they're not related at all. I mainly just find myself ignoring that they're stepsiblings, which is fairly easy. Eden and Tyler's romance has really had its ups and downs throughout this series, but I really liked where this book took their romance. I liked seeing how hard Tyler had worked to heal himself in this book, and how much he tried to change. I was a bit startled by Eden's dad and how he affected this one, but I'm happy that they reconciled. These books are definitely quick reads, and I really like them when I'm just looking for something I don't have to think about. I'd definitely recommend this for romance readers!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492632214" href="/book/show/28321049-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8563233-sophie?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1457884109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16632287965756911412">I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher via NetGalley. This in no way impacted on my view.<br/><br/>After the truth came out about Eden and Tyler's relationship, Tyler left Eden to deal with the fallout. A pariah in her own family, she's dreading returning to LA to face everyone. Her life in Chicago at college is going great, and she would love more than anything to hide out there for the summer, but she knows she'll have to face it all eventually. When Ella organises for a family trip to Sac</span>
  <span id="freeText16632287965756911412" style="display:none">I received an Advance Reader Copy from the publisher via NetGalley. This in no way impacted on my view.<br /><br />After the truth came out about Eden and Tyler's relationship, Tyler left Eden to deal with the fallout. A pariah in her own family, she's dreading returning to LA to face everyone. Her life in Chicago at college is going great, and she would love more than anything to hide out there for the summer, but she knows she'll have to face it all eventually. When Ella organises for a family trip to Sacramento, with all the family, including Tyler, Tyler finally sees just what Eden's been suffering sine he left, and they decide to leave, and go to Portland - Eden's old hometown, and where Tyler's been for the past year. Tyler is sorry for leaving Eden, and want's nothing more than for them to be together, and in Portland, they finally can be.<br /><br />Tyler and Eden have grown so much throughout this series. In the beginning, they were annoying, and not well thought out, but now they're fully fleshed out characters, and I'm sad to see them go. Eden had a lot of anger at the start of this book - understandably, really - but once she understood why Tyler did what he did, she mellowed, and fell for him all over again. Though Tyler had been gone for a year, that doesn't mean he's been doing nothing. In Portland, he's been working hard on a project of his, and I felt proud of him, as if he was someone I knew. <br /><br />I'm really glad with how the series ended, and am looking forward to reading more from this author in the future.</span>

<div id="review_1692282628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1692282628" />
    <a title="Kristy Mauna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46855210-kristy-mauna"><img alt="Kristy Mauna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600710880p2/46855210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1692282628?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristy Mauna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristy Mauna" href="/user/show/46855210-kristy-mauna">Kristy Mauna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/28076471-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46855210-kristy-mauna?shelf=arc-reading">arc-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46855210-kristy-mauna?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46855210-kristy-mauna?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1692282628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1953820497712153650"><i>Did I Mention I Miss You?</i> is the final book in the DIMILY trilogy. It's by far my favorite book out of the entire series! I thought Estelle Maskame brought Tyler and Eden's story to a beautiful close and I absolutely loved it.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"I guess in a way we're all just broken pieces, hoping somehow to fit together to become a perfect picture, a real family."</i>
</b><br/><br/>The story begins almost a year after Tyler decided to leave behind both Santa Monica and Eden to find his purpose in life. Which brings us back to </span>
  <span id="freeText1953820497712153650" style="display:none"><i>Did I Mention I Miss You?</i> is the final book in the DIMILY trilogy. It's by far my favorite book out of the entire series! I thought Estelle Maskame brought Tyler and Eden's story to a beautiful close and I absolutely loved it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I guess in a way we're all just broken pieces, hoping somehow to fit together to become a perfect picture, a real family."</i>
</b><br /><br />The story begins almost a year after Tyler decided to leave behind both Santa Monica and Eden to find his purpose in life. Which brings us back to Eden and her life right now. She's spent a year away from home, attending college in Chicago, but that doesn't mean that everyone has forgotten about her forbidden relationship with her step-brother. She's still dealing with all of the looks and snickers surrounding her as she's back in Santa Monica for the summer.<br /><br />Tyler is no longer in Eden's life, her relationship with her family is strained, and the only good outcome from all of this is the fact that it's brought her closer to her best friend, Rachael. Let me start off by reminding you that I couldn't stand Eden in the last book. She was selfish, childish, and moody. I hoped that she would redeem herself though and I'm happy to announce that she certainly did! She's a bit lost and insecure at the beginning of the book, but she quickly finds her confidence and strength by sticking up for herself and the things she loves. I could instantly connect to this more mature side of her and was pleased to see how well she grew by the end of the series.<br /><br />As the story progresses, Tyler finds his way back home to Santa Monica and he brings all of the drama. I loved seeing him again though because he's a lot calmer than he was in the last book. . . And definitely more swoon-worthy! We learn the story behind what he's been doing for the past year without Eden and where he's at in his life now. Tyler is probably my favorite character out of this series because he ended up being more than just a moody/typical bad boy. Like Eden, he has truly grown up and developed into a more mature person which made me happy to see.<br /><br />My favorite aspect of this book was the fact that it deals more with their family issues than anything else. Now that their relationship is more established, these two have to work together to build something in a way where it will no longer hurt the people around them. First, I loved Ella and her relationship with both Tyler and Eden. Second, the conversations between Eden and her father completely broke me. It was so important to see all of these relationships unfold and become complicated though. I was so proud of the way they dealt with everything concerning their family.<br /><br />Tyler and Eden's story ends beautifully, and it's full of hope for both of their futures. We see old faces and all of the storylines get wrapped up nicely. There were a few characters that I wish got a reappearance, but I was happy they were at least mentioned in this book. It wraps up nicely where not everything is perfect either, which makes this story both realistic and relatable. I'm happy that Maskame didn't just write a "happily ever after" ending for her characters because it would've felt too rushed. Also, her writing was just as fantastic and continues to grow through each book she writes!<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this book. Unlike the previous books, there was less (pointless) drama and more meaningful moments to drive this story to a close. There were plenty of adorable moments between Tyler and Eden, and great reunions also! <i>DIMIMY</i> was everything I hoped it would be and more! Like always, I recommend this book to anyone who enjoys contemporaries or romance, or if you've read any of the previous books because you are sure to enjoy this one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1953820497712153650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1814324122" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1814324122" />
    <a title="Ari " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39598773-ari"><img alt="Ari " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577904181p2/39598773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1814324122?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari " href="/user/show/39598773-ari">Ari </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/28076471-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814324122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3668458979065776899"><b>
  <i>Original review: <a href='https://thedaydreamingbookworm.com/2016/12/05/did-i-mention-i-miss-you-by-estelle-maskame/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Daydreaming Bookworm</a><br/><br/>*I received an ARC from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.*</i>
</b><br/><br/>When it comes to reading experiences, <i>The DIMILY Trilogy</i> is on my list as being one of the “more interesting reading experience” I have ever had. I initially went into the series with low expectations, mainly because this is a step-sibling romance and I’m not too fond of those. I was not too impressed with the first installment, but I was still curious to see where things were goi</span>
  <span id="freeText3668458979065776899" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Original review: <a href="https://thedaydreamingbookworm.com/2016/12/05/did-i-mention-i-miss-you-by-estelle-maskame/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Daydreaming Bookworm</a><br><br>*I received an ARC from the publisher in exchange for an honest review.*</i>
</b><br><br>When it comes to reading experiences, <i>The DIMILY Trilogy</i> is on my list as being one of the “more interesting reading experience” I have ever had. I initially went into the series with low expectations, mainly because this is a step-sibling romance and I’m not too fond of those. I was not too impressed with the first installment, but I was still curious to see where things were going to go, so I picked up the sequel and was absolutely loving it…until it ended with a major cliffhanger that had me cursing up a storm. Going into the final installment, I was still pretty pissed, but I was hoping the final installment would redeem this series for me. Luckily, it did!<br><br>It’s been one year since Eden Munro last saw her stepbrother, Tyler Bruce. After having to deal with the aftermath of the mess they’ve made on her own, Eden wants nothing more than to move on from Tyler and escape all the whispers about their forbidden love. But when Tyler returns hoping to explain himself, will Eden hear him out, or will she be the one to walk away this time.<br><br><b>WHAT AN EMOTIONAL ROLLER COASTER!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480950972ra/21368014.gif" width="300" height="175" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For someone who started out initially not loving <i>The DIMILY Trilogy</i>, I got to say this series and these characters have grown on me the past few months and I’m happy that I gave this series a chance instead of just stopping at the first book. I went into this book not loving Eden’s character at all. She annoyed me so much in the previous installments, mainly because she only ever reacted to the things that were going on around her instead of stepping up and expressing how she truly felt, and I was afraid that she would be the same way in this book. But thankfully she found her voice and she was not putting up with anyone’s BS, especially Tyler’s. As for Tyler, <b>I FREAKIN’ LOVED HIM</b>! His development has got to be one of the best I’ve seen and I love how he turned his life around and worked on his issues to better himself, <b>FOR HIMSELF</b> and not for anyone else. These two have come a long way from when we first met them and I have loved watching them grow, as they made mistakes and learned from those mistakes, which ultimately lead them to having a happier relationship. <br><br>While I loved many things about this book, there were a few things that didn’t sit well with me. First thing being Eden’s father. I hate this man so much and he is honestly not redeemable in my eyes. Any father who treats their own daughter like that should be ashamed to call themselves a father in the first place! The second thing is that I felt like this book was a bit too short. There was a lot of tension in the beginning of this book between all the characters and I felt like all that tension just easily disappeared by the end. There were a few issues towards the end that I felt needed to be better clarified, although I won’t say what they were since they are major spoilers! Also, considering Tyler was gone for a year, Eden forgave him within a matter of days and I wish she hadn’t forgiven him so quickly. I’m all for resolving conflicts, but quick fixes aren’t always best way to handle them.<br><br>All in all, I am very happy with the way the DIMILY series ended. <b>MY FAVES GOT THE HAPPINESS THEY DESERVE AND I AM CRYING!</b> I seriously didn’t expect the tears at the end and I really just want to reread this series from the beginning and experience all the feels again! Even though I am going to miss this series, I’m excited to see what Estelle Maskame writes next and hopefully I will love those books as much as I loved this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3668458979065776899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1721280813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1721280813" />
    <a title="Dee☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7100759-dee"><img alt="Dee☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569962724p2/7100759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1721280813?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dee☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dee☾" href="/user/show/7100759-dee">Dee☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781492632214" href="/book/show/28321049-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7100759-dee?shelf=contemporary-fluff">contemporary-fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7100759-dee?shelf=give-me-that-boy">give-me-that-boy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1721280813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14739376004651353789"> <br/>PERFECT ENDING! Everything I wanted and more. I loved the acceptance, finally. The growing relationships and our passionate romance. I am really going to miss these characters I love so much.<br/><br/>Tyler has some of the best character development that I have seen in a Contemporary novel. You wouldn't even be able to recognize him in book 3 as opposed to him in book 1. I couldn't stand him in DIMILY and I am so, so proud of the man he is because he worked so hard to get to where he is. Everything he is</span>
  <span id="freeText14739376004651353789" style="display:none"> <br />PERFECT ENDING! Everything I wanted and more. I loved the acceptance, finally. The growing relationships and our passionate romance. I am really going to miss these characters I love so much.<br /><br />Tyler has some of the best character development that I have seen in a Contemporary novel. You wouldn't even be able to recognize him in book 3 as opposed to him in book 1. I couldn't stand him in DIMILY and I am so, so proud of the man he is because he worked so hard to get to where he is. Everything he is doing and the man he is striving to be was just so beautiful and I wanted to cry and hug him because he's a beautiful person. I am so glad that he is able to see that. I think I burst into tears when he told Eden's dad at the end "I'm a good guy." (<b>SO MANY FEELS</b>) <br /><br />As for Eden, she really bothered me in the beginning. She was so angry and full of rage that I just couldn't connect with her. Yes I understood she resentment but I felt like she was being too unfair to Tyler. He was working hard and she just kept placing so much blame on him. I am glad that she woke up finally and became the forgiving, understanding Eden that was supportive. <br /><br />Ella and Karen were so accepting and wonderful. Dave and Jamie were both assholes and I wanted someone to just punch them in the face. They deserved it. <br /><br />I had a few issues here and there, but overall it was fantastic and I'm happy. ❤️</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3580635934223722632">I have been waiting for this book since I had first picked up Did I Mention I Love You. I absolutely loved book one and two, don't get me wrong the third book was good but I really didn't think it was all that great. I felt like it was a little lagged, I didn't feel that same connection with Tyler and Eden like I did in the other books.   <span id="freeText3580635934223722632" style="display:none">I have been waiting for this book since I had first picked up Did I Mention I Love You. I absolutely loved book one and two, don't get me wrong the third book was good but I really didn't think it was all that great. I felt like it was a little lagged, I didn't feel that same connection with Tyler and Eden like I did in the other books. There was a lot that happened which is why I felt it was a little rushed and a little to much, since live in So Cal and she absolutely went hard on Santa Monica but kinda made nice towards the end. I get its home but whoa. lol. the one thing I was extremely upset about in the end was (MAY BE A SPOILER?) the never actually said I love you( like I always wanted them to!) but Eden in her head is thinking, "I am so in love with him" instead they say it in French and Spanish so I was really hoping that they would finally tell each other, disappointing. I was happy they made peace with family and Tiffany had no involvement :) but I guess I wanted more than what the ending that was given. And i also just had so much higher expectations.</span>

  <span id="freeText11604832627563421068" style="display:none">*I receive this book in exchange for an honest review * <br /><br />Probably for the fans of the series DIMILY it was a long time waiting for this book, but I think it was worth the wait, even though I have not read the previous books, it was worth it. <br /><br /> Story is well written (I have to make up for the previous two), then I think that is a great DIMIMY the end of the story of Eden &amp; Tyler. <div id="review_1712769307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712769307" />
    <a title="elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36538861-elle"><img alt="elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599198294p2/36538861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712769307?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elle" href="/user/show/36538861-elle">elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/26251365-did-i-mention-i-miss-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36538861-elle?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1712769307&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712769307" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4798995121598023840">★★★★<br/>I think I actually love how this ended. I'm one of the people who'd read the wattpad version of the trilogy long before I got to this one, and I really loved this version. I loved the whole concept of Tyler improving each book. He was such a great character, and it was a pleasure reading about his character development. Although I'm definitely one for angst, I loved how mellow the last book was because it showed that Eden and Tyler have matured from all the petty drama that happened in high </span>
  <span id="freeText4798995121598023840" style="display:none">★★★★<br />I think I actually love how this ended. I'm one of the people who'd read the wattpad version of the trilogy long before I got to this one, and I really loved this version. I loved the whole concept of Tyler improving each book. He was such a great character, and it was a pleasure reading about his character development. Although I'm definitely one for angst, I loved how mellow the last book was because it showed that Eden and Tyler have matured from all the petty drama that happened in high school. I also love how Estelle took the book in the direction of co-dependence, and how Tyler felt the need to stray away from Eden for a while to find himself. And how he returned once he was confident that he had. I also love how Estelle didn't tie all the loose knots; she left us wondering. Eden's relationship with her dad was never really fixed in the end, just amended. Tyler's relationship with Ella was such a great one, and I think it was one of the best mother-son relationships I've read in a long time. I think this trilogy definitely touched on sensitive issues - abuse, drugs, high school drama, manipulative relationships, and codependence in the subtlest but greatest way possible.<br />I loved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4798995121598023840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3121748194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14602927794537574150"><strong>Amazing!</strong><br/><br/>I have enjoyed going on this journey with these characters from the beginning to the end. I have read their struggles and watched them grow. I will say that at the end of the 2nd book I was pretty upset about some events that unfolded but as I was reading through this book it hit me. This is what life is. It's not always pretty and sometimes things dont go the way we expect them to. People get hurt and yeah it sucks but it's all a part of life. I felt for everyone as they went through th</span>
  <span id="freeText14602927794537574150" style="display:none"><strong>Amazing!</strong><br /><br />I have enjoyed going on this journey with these characters from the beginning to the end. I have read their struggles and watched them grow. I will say that at the end of the 2nd book I was pretty upset about some events that unfolded but as I was reading through this book it hit me. This is what life is. It's not always pretty and sometimes things dont go the way we expect them to. People get hurt and yeah it sucks but it's all a part of life. I felt for everyone as they went through their ups and downs and all in all it was an amazing ride. <br /><br />Estelle- you rock! You wrote an amazing story with one heck of a storyline. It couldnt of been easy but it was raw and true! Definitely worth 5 stars!<br /><br />I'm sad to see this come to an end but I'm looking forward to the 10 years later book! </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gvR3Rkd33alIBsQytO6OUyQLaTLda5m4wL9q6n+9DS8rR8uZaJLHoGE4efowjat8ZqjOwEDNMtTLWpF+VCoPCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('K5N+Q8DUUvgTK1WI5kdWB06oUDlcfAUgDQ1iXozBPjeCIMKc7zFI8ToV6EBiJHMoDAv3y8HarkwG6JnKp1Y8EA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3918432698255492148">Estelle Maskame is a novelist from Peterhead in Scotland. After gaining universal acclaim online during her teenage years, she signed a print contract with the Edinburgh-based publisher Black & White Publishing at the age of seventeen. She left school and now writes full-time. Did I Mention I Love You? is her first novel. </span>

After gaining universal acclaim online during her teenage years, she signed a print contract with the Edinburgh-based publisher Black &amp; White Publishing at the age of seventeen. She left school and now writes full-time. Did I Mention I Love You? is her first novel. </span>

(DIMILY, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7745429.Estelle_Maskame?origin=series_works\">Estelle Maskame<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.91 avg rating &mdash; 23,135 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2015\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5568992415815520389\">When sixteen-year-old Eden Munro agrees to spend the summer with her estranged father in the beachfront city of Santa Monica, California, she has no idea what she’s letting herself in for. Eden\'s parents are divorced and have gone their separate ways<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5568992415815520389\" style=\"display:none\">When sixteen-year-old Eden Munro agrees to spend the summer with her estranged father in the beachfront city of Santa Monica, California, she has no idea what she’s letting herself in for. Eden\'s parents are divorced and have gone their separate ways, and now her father has a brand new family. For Eden, this means she\'s about to meet three new step-brothers. The eldest of the three is Tyler Bruce, a troubled teenager with a short temper and a huge ego. Complete polar opposites, Eden quickly finds herself thrust into a world full of new experiences as Tyler\'s group of friends take her under their wing.
